Transmitting a Communication, dated March 2, 2000 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I hereby appoint Dr. Bradley Langer as Interim Medical Director at Cook County Hospital, replacing Dr.
Stephen Hamburger who recently resigned.
I submit this communication for your approval.

837

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

In accordance with Rule 2-10, Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to
suspend the rules to consider the appointment of Dr. Bradley Langer. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the appointment by the President be
approved. The motion carried unanimously.

REAPPOINTMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 9, 2000 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I hereby reappoint Mr. Howard Brookins to the Cook County Department of Corrections Board for a term
to begin immediately and expire January I, 2005.
I submit this communications for your approval.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved that the appointment by the President be
approved. The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated February 22, 2000 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
Respectfully request approval of proposed amendments to the Human Resources Ordinance, which
currently serves as the blueprint for the Bureau's duties and responsibilities.
Several amendments are "form" in nature, adding a section heading numbering system and subsections.
There are also minor text amendments inserting words or reordering sentence structures for grammatical
purposes.
The primary substantive amendments provide for transiti on to the Human Resources "Career Service"
system from "Civil Service"; distinguish Career Service from other Human Resources functions, s uch as
benefits ad ministration, salary administration, etc.; clarify the application of prior handbooks, rules,
guides, etc., which, over the years, have been used by employees and recognized by cou11s as applicable
unless repealed; and clarify the application of by-laws, state licensing board and accrediting organizations
to selection and discipline of physicians and dentists.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

ORDINANCE AMENDING
BUREAU OF HUMAN RESOURCES ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Illinois is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to
A11icle VII, Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and pursuant to the authority therein granted,
may exercise any power and perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and

838

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule powers, on November +e 12., 1992, the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County adopted an Ordinance creating the Bureau of Human Resources to
establish a professional and progressive merit-based human resources management system and to
administer human resource functions; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County determines that it is necessary to make
certain amendments to such Ordinance and to further provide for transition and implementation of such
Ordinance;
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED by the Board of Commissioners of the County of
Cook, lllinois, as follows:

ARTICLE ONE

The November .J-612., 1992, Ordinance establishing the Bureau of Human Resources is hereby
amended as set forth below by insertion of underlined text and deletion ofstricken text:
Section 1.

PURPOSE

It is the general purpose of this Ordinance, and 1t 1s necessary in the public interest, to establish a
professional and progressive merit-based human resource management system that: ( 1) attracts, retains
and motivates competent County employees; (2) provides the President and other County executives with
the necessary flexibility and management control to assure the delivery of quality public service and (3)
establishes fair, equitable procedures for employees and applicants for employment.

Section 2.

ESTABLISHMENT OF THE BUREAU OF HUMAN RESOURCES

A.

There is hereby established a Bureau which shall be known as the Bureau of Human Resources.
The C hief of Human Resources shall be the chief executive officer of the Bureau of Human
Resources and shall be appointed by the President and shall serve at the pleasure of the President.
The Chief of Human Resources shall be responsible for the general management and control of
the Bureau Human Resources in a manner consistent with the ordinances of the County, the laws
of the state, and the rules of the Bureau.

B.

The Chief of Human Resources shall have the power and duty to:
(I)

Encourage and exercise leadership in the development of effective human resources
management within the several departments in the County service, and to make available
the faci lities of the Bureau of Human Resources to this end ;

(2)

Advise department heads, including elected officials, and the budget director as to the
correct classification of a position before it is included in the budget and before an
appointment is made. No appointment shall be approved without the prior approval of
the Chief of Hum an Resources as to the classification of the position;

(3)

Foster and develop~ @1 programs f.or the iA1provement of eA1plo~·ee effeetiveness for the
administration of human resource functions including position classification, salary
administration, employee benefits, collective bargaining, labor management relations,
employee communications, safety and health for the employees in all County
departments including departments headed by elected officials; and , ans also, inel1:18ing
b1:1t not limitee to, (Q1 programs for a professional and progressive merit based system for

programs for recruitment, selection, discipline, grievance, promotion, affirmative action,
performance management, probationary periods and trainin& , for eA'lployees 1:1nder the

data;

(5)

Certify that persons named on every payroll have been appointed and employed in
accordance with the current budget; in addition, for employees under the direction and
control of the President certify that persons named on payrolls have been appointed and
employed in accordance with the provisions of this Ordinance and the rules adopted
thereunder. No disbursing or auditi ng officer shall make or approve or take any part in
making or approving any payment for personnel service to those persons holding a
position in the County service unless said payroll voucher or account of such pay bears
the certification of the Chief of Human Resources or his/her authorized agent;

(6)

Apply and carry out this ordinance and the rules thereunder and perform any other lawful
acts which may be necessary or desirable to carry out the purpose and provisions of this

(7)

Section 3.

EXEMPTIONS

The Bureau of Human Resources Ordinance and the Human Resources Management System thereby
created, shall be construed as the law regulating the civil services of Cook County for all purposes
including Section 17 of the Cook County Forest Preserve Act (70 ILCS 810/17) except as herein
exempted. There shall be three categories of exemption from the provisions of this Ordinance.
A.

Fifst;--t Ihe following positions shall be exempt from the classification authority of the Chief of

Human Resources and from the seleetion Career Service provisions of this ordinance.
Elected officials;
Bureau Chiefs;
Executive heads of departments;
Members of boards and commissions.

( I)
(2)
(3)
(4)

B.

Seeond, t The following positions shall be exempt only from the Career Service and the seleetion
provisions of this ordinance; these positions shall be subject to classification and all other
provisions of the ordinance:
( 1)

Employees working directly for the County Board and its various committees;

(2)

Employees working in the office of the President, and employees in the offices of the
Bureau Chiefs and the Department of Capital Planning and Policy;

840

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
(3)

Employees of departments directly or indirectly headed by an elected official other than
the President;

(4)

~mployees wl'lose work is seasonal and does not exceed 150 da)' in any caleRdar yeaF;
Employees whose position has been designated as an exempt position pursuant to the
Judgment in the matter of Michael L. Shakman, et al., vs. The Democratic Organization
of Cook County, et al., 69 C 2145 entered on January 7, 1994 in the United States District
Court for the Northern District of Illinois, Eastern Division.

(5)

Employees designated as executive service because they are responsible for the
development of departmental management policy or because their positions are at the
nexus where policy and implementation meet and are therefore, essential to the
successful implementation of policy;

(6)

Positions exempted from the career service pursuant to the rules of the Bureau upon
recommendation of a department head and after comment and recommendation by the
Chief of Human Resources and the approval of the President. These additional
exemptions must be based on the need for flexibility in appointment to positions which
(a) are necessary in order to maintain confidentiality or (b) are administratively
necessary in order to effect a program including, but not limited to, such programs as
internships, student work experience programs, trainee programs, federal public service
employment programs, and any other programs, which, because of the program
requirements, cannot be subject to career service requirements.

All employees exempted in the above category are considered to be "at will " employees and shall serve at
the pleasure of the appointing authority unless otherwise provided for by law or contract.

Section 4.

HUMAN RESOURCE RULES

A.
The Chief of Human Resources shall issue rules to implement the provisions of this Ordinance.
Prior to the effective date of such rules, the Chief of Human Resources shall give public notice in one or
more newspapers of general circulation, and in no case shall such publication be less than I 0 days before
the effective date of the proposed rule or amendment to the rule. Such public notice shall include
information concerning where the rules can be reviewed and where comments may be directed. Nothing
contained herein shall prohibit the Chief of Human Resources from giving other appropriate public
notice. The rules shall provide for:
( 1)

The preparation, maintenance and revi sion of a pos1hon classification plan for all
positions, except those exempted in Section 3 of this Ordinance based upon similarity of
duties performed and responsibility assigned, so that the same qualifications may
reasonably be required for and the same schedule of pay may be applied equitably to all
positions in the same class;

(2)

The annual submission of a pay plan to the President;

(3)

The recruitment of persons in the Career Service on the basis of their relati >'e fitAess
qualifications. Whenever it is appropriate in the judgment of the Chief of Human
Resources a fair and open lottery procedure may be applied to develop the order of
candidates to be considered for selection. Other selection procedures including, but not
limited to interviews, performance tests, or medical examinations may be applied;

(4)

The establishment of lists of eligibles for appointment and promotion in Career Service,
upon which lists shall be placed the names of successful candidates in order of their
relative excellence in the respective examinations, where such examinations are
administered. The Chief of Human Resources may substitute categorical rankings such
as excellent, well qualified and qualified for numerical rating and establish eligible lists
accordingly. Such rules may provide for lists by area or location, by department or other
agency, for removal of those not available for or refusing employment, for minimum and
maxi mum duration of such li sts, for the addition of names of successful candidates to list
and for s uch other provisions as may be necessary to provide rapid and satisfactory
service to the operating agencies. The rules may authorize removal of eligibles from lists
if those eligibles fail to furnish evidence of availability upon forms sent to them by the
Chief of Hum an Resources;

(5)

The certification to an appointing authority the names.;-faJ of a minimum of 4J:te seven
persons, or all applicants if less than seven apply, (a) with the highest numerical ratings
available on the appropriate eligible list to fill each vacancy, or (b) from the highest
ranking group if the list is by categorical ranking instead of numerical ratings;

(6)

Promotions which shall give appropriate considerations to the applicant's qualifications,
record of performance and ability;

(7)

Probationary periods after original appointment not to exceed one year. An employee
who complete a probationary period shall have the status of a career service employee;

Probationary periods after promotional appointment not to exceed one year. The ru les

The establishment of disciplinary measures such as suspension, demotion in rank or

of the charges on which discipline is based, together with an explanation of the evidence
supporting the charges and an opportunity for the employee to respond to the charges in
writing before action is taken, appeals after such disciplinary action, and a hearing on the
charges upon request of the employee in case of discharge, demotion or suspension
exceeding I0 work days, consistent with the requirement of due process of law. The
charges and explanation of evidence need not be in any particular form , but must be
suffic ient to apprize the employee of the matters on which discipline may be based. The
em ployee's response must be reviewed by the department head or designee responsible
for making the decision, provided that such designee may be the person who initiated the
charges against the employee. No career service employee may be discharged, demoted
or suspended for more than I0 work days unless the statement of charges and any matter
in support are first reviewed by the Chief of Human Resources, before the employee is
notified of such action;

( 14)

Development and operations of programs to improve work effectiveness, including
training, education, safety, health, welfare, counseling, recreation and employee relations.

Section 5.

EMPLOYEE APPEALS BOARD

There is hereby created an Employee Appeals Board consisting of three five members appointed by the
President of the County Board for a term of six years, or until their respective successors are appointed
and qualified, except that of the initially appointed board, one member shall be appointed for two years,
eRe two members sha ll be appointed for four years, and eRe two members for six years. Upon the
expiration of the term of any member of the personnel board Employee Appeals Board, the President
shall appoint each successor for a term of six years and each member shall serve until a successor is
appointed and qualified. A vacancy shall be filled for the remainder of an unexpired term in the same
manner as original appointments. The President shall appoint one of the members of the board as
chairperson to serve for a term of two years or until a successor is appointed. The President may, in the
President's discretion, remove any member of the Employee Appeals Board for incompetence, neglect of
duty or malfeasance in office. The President shall forthwith notify the County Board in writing of any
such removal. Any vacancy created by such removal by the President s hall be filled by the President
pursuant to the provision of this Section.
In addition to the duties described in Section 6, the Employee Appeals Board may be requested by the
President or by the Chief of Human Resources to prepare special reports or to otherwise give advice on
human resource issues.

Section 6.

HEARING OF
EMPLOYEES

Cl=IARGBS

DISCIPLINARY ACTIONS

BROUGHT AGAINST

A.
The Employee Appeals Board, a member thereof, or a hearing officer appointed by the Board
shall conduct a hearing of all appeals by any Career Service employee not represented by a union, of
discharge, demotion, or suspension for a period of more than I 0 days upon request of the employee. The
Chief of Human Resources aAtl may provide by rule for review of suspensions of 10 days or less. The
Employee Appeals Board, any of its members, or a hearing officer appointed by the Board may
administer oaths and secure by notice both the evidence and witnesses for the production of relevant
books and papers. All proceedings before the Board, a member thereof, or the hearing officer shall be
recorded. The findings and decision of a member of the Board or hearing officer shall be certified to the
Employee Appeals Board, which may accept or reject the findings and decision or may require further
hearing before the Board. After the Board accepts the findings and decision of its member or hearing
officer, or after a hearing, the Employee Appeals Board shall certify the findings and decision to the Chief
of Human Resources who shall then notify the appropriate appointing authority. Nothing in this Section
limits the power of the appointing authority or his/her designee to take di sci plinary action against a
subordinate purs uant to the rules of the Bureau of Human Resources.
B.
Appeals by an employee of discharge, demotion or suspension for a period exceeding I 0 days
shall be governed by the following procedure:
(I)

The employee shall be given written notice of the disciplinary decision by the department
head or designee. The employee may appeal the department head's or designee's
decision to the Employee Appeals Board by making a written request therefor within five
calendar days of the effective date of discipline. An appeal shall not affect the effective
date of discipline.

844

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
(2)

If the employee requests a hearing, a date therefore shall be set, not more than 45 days
following receipt of the request for hearing by the Employee Appeals Board. Either party
may request a continuance for good cause shown, but the hearing must be completed
within 60 calendar days of the initial hearing date. If the time limitations provided for
herein are not met due to delay requested by or caused by the County, the employee shall
be entitled prospectively to the pay and benefits of the position held before the
imposition of suspension or discharge, or in the case of a demotion the difference in pay
between the former and current positions, beginning with the first day after the failure to
meet the time limit, pending decision of the Employee Appeals Board, but the employee
shall have no right to be reinstated except by order of the Employee Appeals Board. The
Employee Appeals Board shall file a written report in all cases where a discharged,
demoted or suspended employee becomes entitled to the pay and benefits of his or her
former position prospectively by reason of failure to meet a time limit. The report shall be
filed with the County Board within 21 days of the failure to meet a time limit, and shall
contain the causes and circumstances of such failure. Nothing herein shall deprive the
employee Appeals Board of jurisdiction to decide the merits of the disciplinary action.

(3)

An employee whose di scipline is not upheld shall receive full back pay for any period
when he or she was off work, or serving in a lower position, less any lesser disciplinary
action imposed by the Board. Said employee shall be reinstated to his or her position or
such lower position as determined by the Board, upon notification of the Board' s
decision, or following such lesser discipline as may be imposed by the Board, as
appropriate.

Section 7.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURES FOR EMPLOYEES

The Chief of Human Resources shall prescribe uniform procedures for pursuing grievances for Career
Service employees not represented b)' a 1:1nion where such grievance procedures are not provided in a
collective bargaining agreement, including provisional employees. "Grievances," as defined herein shall
not include disputes over salary scales, reclassification or wage rates.

Section 9.

NON-DISCRJMINA TION

No person shall discriminate against any County employee or applicant for County employment because
of race, color, sex, age, religion, disability, national origin, ancestry, sexual orientation, marital status,
parental status, military discharge status, source of income, er housing, or any other protected category
established by law, statute or ordinance.

Section 10.

UNLAWFUL PRA CTICES RELATING TO EMPLOYEES AND EMPLOYMENT PENALTY

A.
No person shall directly or indirectly coerce, attempt to coerce or command any employee in the
County service to pay, lend or contribute anything of value to a party, committee, organization, agency, or
person for political purposes. Nothing herein contained shall affect the ri ght of the employee to hold
membership in, and support, a political party or candidate, to vote as he/she chooses, to express his/her
opinions on all political subjects and candidates, to maintain political neutrality, and to attend political
meetings.
B.
No persons shall make any fal se statement, certificate, mark, rating or report with regard to any
test, certification or appointment made under any provisions of this Ordinance or in any manner commit
or attempt to commit any fraud , prevent the impartia l execution of this Ordinance and any rules issues
thereunder.

C.
No person shall , directly or indirectly, give, re nder, pay, offer, solicit, or accept any money,
service or other valuable consideration for any appointment, proposed appointment, promotion or
proposed promotion, or any advantage in a position in the County service.
No em ployee of the Bureau of Human Resource, examiner, or other person shall deceive or
D.
obstruct any person in his/her right to examination, eligibility, certification or appointment under this
Ordinance, or furnish to any person special or secret information for the purpose of affecting the rights of
any person with respect to employment in the career service.
E.
Any person who willfully violates this section shall be fined not less than $100 nor more than $500
or be imprisoned for not more than 6 months, or both . Any person who is found to be in violation of this
section shall , for a period of five years, be ineligible for appointment to or employment in a position in the
County service, and if he/she is an officer or employee of the County shall forfeit his/her office or pos ition.

B.

The following transition schedule shall apply to employee discipl inary matters:

All disciplinary matters pending before the Civil Service Commission o n the effective

Human Resources Ordinance.

An employee holding a temporary appointment in a c ivi l service pos1t1on fo r one year or more
immediately prior to the adoption of this Ordinance sha ll have Career Service status in that Position
without further exam ination, unless separated as pro·,.ided b~' ordinanee or rule, or unless the position is
otherwise reelassified, realloeated or exempted from career service as provided by this Ordinance.
Any employee holding a temporary appointment in a civi l service position for less than one year
immediately prior to the adoption of this Amendatory Ordinance shall be required to serve a probationary
period of one year commencing on the date of the employee's temporary appointment to that position.
Upon the s uccessful completi on of any such probationary period, said employee shall have Career Service
status in that position without further examination, unless separated as provided by ordinance or rule, or
unless the position is otherwise rec lassified, reallocated or exempted from Career Service as provided by
this Ordinance. Any employee covered under the provisions of a collective bargaining contract will be
subject to the probationary period found in that contract rather than the provisions of this Ordinance.

RECIPROCAL AGREEMENTS WITH OTHER AGENCIES

The Chief of Human Resources is authorized and empowered to enter into reciprocal agreements, upon
s uch terms as may be agreed upon, for the use of equipment, materials, faci lities, with any public agency
or body for purposes deemed of benefit to the County service. The Chief of Human Resources may
cooperate with other governmental agencies in conducting personnel tests, classification of positions,
recruiti ng personnel and training personnel.

COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Cook County Firearm Training Certification
T his Ordinance may be cited as the Cook County Firearms Training Certification Ordinance.
Cook County and other counties throughout Illinois and the United States have experienced
incidents of violent crimes involving firearms, specifically, handguns.
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to protect the health, safety
and welfare of the citizens of Cook County, and

848

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
WHEREAS, unintentional firearm injuries and death occur each year due to a lack of proper
training in the handling and storage of firearms. According to the Center for Disease Control's National
Center for Injury Prevention unintentional firearm deaths in the nation have historically accounted for as
much as 58% of firearm deaths of persons between the ages of I 0-29 years, and
WHEREAS, current Illinois Law requires for the purchase of firearms and ammunition that the
purchaser possess a valid Firearm Owner Identification Card (FOID). The current law is silent on the
purchaser's competency and ability to handle a firearm in safe and proper manner, and
WHEREAS, firearms, especially handguns, are a major contributor to incidents of death and
permanent injury to the general citizenry and contributes to the increase and spiraling cost to the
taxpayers of Cook County (i.e., healthcare, law enforcement and the judicial system), it is in the best
interest of the citizenry that firearm owners be required to complete a certified course in firearms training.
NOW THEREFORE, PURSUANT TO THE HOME RULE AUTHORITY OF TH E COOK
COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS AS VESTED IN IT BY THE ILLINOIS CONSTITUTION,
BE IT ORDAINED:
That it is in the best interest of the public that purchasers of firearms in Cook County shall prior
to the purchase of a firearm have completed a Certified Firearm Training Course wh ich must have been
taught by a Certified Firearms Instructor.
a) The firearms instructor shall have completed and have been certified by the Illinois Law
Enforcement Training Standards Board or an equivalent recogni zed training and certification
organization;
b) The course, at a minimum shall be an 8 hour course, which shall include instructions in safe
hand Iing, storage and current law effecting firearms and ammunition purchase and proper
transportation of firearms;
c)

Upon an applicants completion of the Firearm Training Course the instructor shall issue to the
applicant a certificate stating that the applicant has completed the Firearms Training Course and
that he/she is qualified to handle a firearm in a safe and proper manner.
ARTICLE I GENERAL PROVISIONS
Title

Section 1-1

This ordinance shall be known as the "Cook County Firearm Training Certification
Ordinance."
Applicability

Section 1-2
(a) This ordinance shall control both the sale and purchase of firearms to the genera l
purchasing public within Cook County except in home rule municipalities which have a separate
municipal ordinance specifically regulating firearms safety training and purchase of firearms.
(b) Pursuant to Article VII, Section 6(c) of the 1970 Constitution ofthe State of Illinois,
if this ordinance confl icts with an ordinance of a home rule municipality, the municipal ordinance shall
prevail within its jurisdiction.

849

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

Severability
Section 1-3
If any section, s ubsection, paragraph, sentence or c lause of thi s ordinance or the
application thereof to any person is for any reason deemed to be invalid or unconstitutional, such decision
shall not affect, impair or invalidate any remaining section, subsection, paragraph, sentence or c lause
hereof or the application of this ordinance to any other person.
Effective Date
Section 1-4

This ordinance sha ll take effect immediately upon passage and publication.

ARTICLE II
Definitions
Section 2-1
a)

As used in the Cook County Firearm Training Certification Ordinance:

Firearms Training shall mean a course taught by a Certified Firearms Instructor. The Certified
Instructor shall have completed the lli inoi s Law Enforcement Training and Standards Board 40
hour training course.

b) Firearm Training Course shall mean a course consisting of a minimum of 8 hours training
comprised of instructions in safe handling of a firearm, safe storage of a firearm and the various
laws applicable to possession of a firearm, ammunition and transportation of firearms.
c) The Certificate of Training shall express that the applicant has completed the requ ired hours of
training and that the named party has demonstrated his or her competency in the safe handling of
firearms and that he/she is qualified to purchase a firearm.
d) Nothing in this ordinance shall entitle a person who has completed a Certified Firearms Training
Course to purchase a firearm if he/she does not possess a current valid Firearms Owners
Identification Card or has not complied with any other existing Federal, State, County, or other
local (municipal) law then in effect.

Section 3-1

Minimum Course Requirements:

The course shall be designed to provide the indi vidual with specific and definiti ve information
regarding shotguns, rifles and handguns. Safety shall be the fundamental focus of the course and s ha ll be
stressed throughout the required hours of instructions.
Course objectives shall at a minimum include the following:
a) The diffe rent types of shotguns, rifles and handguns
b) The parts of a shotgun, rifle and handgun shall be taught.
c) The methods of safe storage and c leaning techniques for shotguns, rifles, handguns and
ammunition shall be stressed
d) Federa l and State laws that pertain to firearms sha ll be taug ht.

850

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

conviction, I am not currently under indictment or prosecution for any offense, and I am not wanted for
questioning or arrest by any Jaw enforcement or govern ment agency . I further state that I do not have a
history of mental illness or substance abuse. I agree to submit my fingerprints to the Sheriff of Cook
County for determination of my civil and criminal background and history. l understand that my training

Transmitting a Communication, dated February 23, 2000 from
RUTH M. ROTHSTEIN, Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with St. Elizabeth's Hospital,
Chicago, Illinois.
This contract would provide an opportunity for patients receiving prenatal care at the Logan Square
Health Center to deli ver newborns at St. Elizabeth's Hospital. The Bureau's physicians and nurse
midwives practicing at the Logan Square Health Center would obtain privileges and have the option to
deliver their patients at St. Elizabeth's Hospital, maintaining continuity of care for patients.
Through this contract Maternal Fetal Medicine physicians will use clinic space at St. Elizabeth's Hospital
to provide outpatient high risk obstetric services. In add ition, St. Elizabeth's Hospital will provide
community education, screening and health services, particularly bilingual diabetes education services, at
the Logan Square Health Center.
This contract provides an opportunity for a partnership that will provide additional services for patients at
Logan Square Health Center.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Revenue generating: $63,072.00 ($2 1,024.00 per year).
period: April I, 2000 through March 3 1, 2003. Requisition No. 05433106.

OO-R-135

RESOLUTION
RESOL YEO by the Members of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, on behalf of the
County of Cook, is hereby authorize and direct its President to execute, by original signature or his
authorized signature stamp, two (2) copies of a TIERED APPROACH TO CORRECTIVE ACTION
OBJECTIVES (TACO) AGREEMENT with Equilon Enterprises, LLC, submitted hereto and made part

following locations as apart of its Highway Permit process.

February 15, 2000 by the Chicago City Council. This agreement between the City of Chicago and the
County of Cook provides Cook County with $4 million under the Local Law Enforcement Block Grant
(LLEBG) 1998 Spending Plan. These funds must be expended by September 30, 2000.
This Agreement also provides Cook County with $7 million under the LLEBG 1999 Spending Plan. The
funds covered under the 1999 Spending Plan must be expended within twenty-four months of the City of
Chicago's receipt of the 1999 fund s.
These funds require a l 0% cash match.
Submitted is a copy of the Ordinance enacted by the City of Chicago authorizing the Agreement between
the City and the County. Also s ubmitted is a detailed spending plan for each of the years covered. Both
of these plans have been reviewed by the City of Chicago and have been prepared in accordance with the
guidelines established by the U.S. Department of Justice.
Permission is hereby requested by the Judicial Advisory Council to enter into sole source agreements with
the State's Attorney, the Sheriff, the Chief Judge, the Chicago Police Department, the Forest Preserve
District, Suburban Cook County Communities and non-profit organizations providing services pursuant
to the combined operation of Project B.A.D.G.E. (Balanced Approach to Drug and Gang Elim ination) as
outlined in the attachments to this letter.
To ensure fiscal integrity, accurate record keeping, program accountabil ity, and optimal outcomes,
authority hereby requested for the Judicial Advisory Council 's Executive Director to enter into written
agreements prepared by the Cook County State's Attorney to memorialize these safeguards.

CONTRACT
Transm itting a Communication from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
JOHN J. ROBINSON, Undersheriff
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the Institute for Relationa l
Development, of La Jolla, California, to provide gender responsive alcohol and drug treatment training
for security and program operational staff. In addition, the Institute will monitor and evaluate the existing
treatment programs at the Department of Women's Justice Services, for program compliance and quality
assurance.

895

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Reason:

The Institute for Relational Development are internationa lly known as criminal justice
consultants and researchers, specializing in the development and evaluation of drug and alcohol
programs serving girls and women. Because the Cook County Sheriffs Office is pioneering
new concepts in women's treatment programs, it is critical that the curriculum developer
(Institute for Relational Development) train operational/security staff, assess the programs for

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY TREASURER
APPROVAL OF PAYMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 1, 2000 from
MARJA PAPPAS, County Treas urer, Cook County Treasurer's Office
I have been advised by the Purchasing Agent that purchases for printing services (paper, envelopes and
brochures), which are necessary to meet the statutory obligations of this office with regard to the issuance of
the tax bills for first installment 1999 taxes and payable on March 1, 2000, did not follow the procedures
established by the Purchasing Department. Identification of the specific purchases is submitted.
My internal rev iew of the facts and circumstances with regard to this iss ue indicate that members of my
staff, without my knowledge, did not process the necessary information to the Purchasing Department on
a timely basis. This lapse prompted them to act in order to meet the statutory deadlines for the issuance
of the tax bill s. I can assure you this will not happen again.
I have directed my senior staff to closely monitor purchasing requirements and to communicate any
problems to the Purchasing Agent directly, rather than to individual staff members.
I am requesting your approval of payments on the following purchases.

CONTRACTING AND PURCHASING ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY - CHAPTER
10 (PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT).
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance
sponsored by Mike Quigley, County Comm issioner; Co-Sponsored by President John H.
Stroger, Jr., Allan C. Carr, Earlean Collins, John P. Daley, Gregg Goslin, Ted Lechowicz,
Roberto Maldonado, William R. Moran, Joseph Mario Moreno, Herbert T. Schumann, Jr.,
Peter N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and Calvin R. Sutker, County
Commissioners:
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
AN ORDINANCE AMEN DING CHAPTER 10:
THE CONTRACTING AND PURCHASING ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, the landfill space available to the residents of Cook County is expected to
g reatly decline within this decade and the cost of solid waste disposal, is expected to rise
steeply; and
WHEREAS, seven landfills in the Chicago Metropolitan Area. representing 21 % of the
region's capacitv, will close by the end of the year 2000; and
WHEREAS, recyclable products are often less expensive than virgin products across their
whole lifecycle when final disposition costs are considered; and
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ENACTED by the Cook County Board of Commissioners

Chairman Daley announced that the ord inance was re-distributed today because two pages we re missing
when it was o riginally distributed. Chairman Daley also identified that the responses from the Purchasing
Agent to Commissioner Hansen's questions relative to the proposed ordinance was re-distributed on
February 7, 2000.

928

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Hansen asked Patrick McFadden, County Purchasing Agent, fo r a brief overview of the
proposed ordinance amendment.
Mr. McFadden reviewed the contracts for the last twelve months in order to make a determi nation of the
fiscal impact. It was detennined that often the recycled product is less of an expense than a non-recycled
product. The substantive impact was on recycled paper, carpeting and paper manufactured without using
chlorine. The carpeting amounted to an additional expense of $100,000.00, although the carpeting itself
was substantive at $1.4 million worth of carpeting. The paper reflected an add itional $26,000.00 on top
of a spread of $63,000.00 over and above the non-recycled paper. The additional expense for chlorinefree paper was $23,000.00 on top of the $63,000.00 totaling $86,000.00. The net effect of the ord inance
is $ 126,000.00, mostly in carpet and recycled paper manufactured without c hlorine.
Commissioner Hansen stated this expenditure is certainly warranted, especially with respect to chlorinefree paper. Commissioner Hansen asked to be added as a co-sponsor of this Ordinance. He asked how
does the County handle the recycling of the refuse stream coming out of the County? He suggested a
comprehensive look at this refuse stream.
Commissioner Quigley thanked Chainnan Daley because this item is an extension of an ordinance that
was previously passed and sponsored by Chairman Daley, which has brought the County to a 53% rate of
purchasing recycled paper. He thanked Mr. McFadden for his efforts in helping to craft the ordinance.
Commissioner Quigley indicated that there are representati ves present from the Illinois Recycl ing
Coalition and Illinois Recycling Association who are in full support of the ordinance. He noted that The
National Association of Counties' (N ACo) new initiative is " Counties purchasing recycled content." The
County is purchasing recycled content for cost savings, environmental purposes, and job creati on. This
ordinance, Commissioner Quigley stated, will create incentives for new markets. He furt her stated that
seven land-fills in the area will be closing within the next year, and as a result environmental costs and
financial costs wi ll increase. The Commissioner indicated the fastest growi ng part of a municipality's
budget is waste disposal. He stated there is a 25-50% cost reduction if recycling items are taken out of
the waste stream.
Commissioner Sutker stated this is a positive step forward. He indicated there has been a recycling effort
on a regular basis in the Village of Skokie fo r over a decade and it is cost-efficient, useful and serves the
community well. He continued by stating the landfill problem is continuing and that 20% of landfill
capacity will be closing by the end of year 2000.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen moved approval of Item No. 231594.
The motion carried.
Note: For the full text of Item 231594 - An Ordinance Amending Chapter 10: The Contracting and
Purchasing Ordinance of Cook County as it was approved and amended please see the Journal of
Proceedings of February 15, 2000 page 764, 00-0-5.

233735

COOK COUNTY TREASURER, by Michael J. Shine, Chief Deputy Treasurer, transmitting
a Communication, dated January I 0, 2000:
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 99-41-519 with
LASALLE NATIONAL BANK, Chicago, lllinois, to provide lock box services for the first
and second real estate tax installments of fiscal year 2000.
The office has completed a Request for Proposal (RFP) bid process fo r the lock box services
for fiscal year 2000. The office solicited responses from fifty (50) banking institutions
resulting in twelve ( 12) responses. Of the twelve ( 12) responses eleven (11) vendors declined
via a letter and one ( 1) vendor was responsive to the RFP. In general, banks declining
submission of a proposal noted the three (3) following reasons:
I.
2.
3.

Lack of a branch network to provide payment centers.
Lack of an ability to process the volume of payments or to provide specialized
services.
Lack of an abili ty to implement payment processing requi rements.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $360,000.00. Costs w ill be offset through an interest bearing
account. Contract period: February I, 2000 through January 3 1, 200 I. (060 249 AeeouAt).

* Referred to the Committee on Finance on February 2, 2000
C hairman Daley announced that additional backup material had been distributed for Item 233735 from
the Treasurer's Office.
Commissioner Sutker stated the lock box effort has been a success and that this pilot program should be
continued in the future. He asked Tim Dauber, Finance Manager of the Treasurer's Office, if there have
been studies of other counties, such as Lake County, with respect to federally insured banks being sites
fo r any taxpayers to make real estate tax payments.
Mr. Dauber referred the question to Jim Allen, representative of the Treasurer's Office.

93 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Mr. A lien answered there has been research and there are major problems. He noted that the most
significant problem under the Lake County system is the banks do not have to tender the receipts that they
receive from the taxpayers for up to I 0 days. As a result, the banks receive potentially I 0 days interest on
those property taxes. Conservatively, if the interest rate was 5% the County would potentially be ceding
$10 million in interest earnings.
Commiss ioner Sutker asked if Cook County is bound to a I 0 day period with LaSalle National Bank?
Mr. Allen responded no, Cook County is not bound to a ten day period.
Comm issioner Sutker asked how LaSalle National Bank pays interest?
Mr. Allen answered the interest is required to be credited into an interest bearing account.
Commissioner Sutker stated that LaSalle National Bank is earning interest on the County's interest as
well. Commissioner Sutker asked what other major problems exist.
Mr. Allen stated that there is a problem in the document provisions. Currently, in Lake County the banks
involved do not provide any copy of the front of the taxpayer's check. Lake County has run into
problems where there are duplicate payments. Mr. Allen received information from Lake County
Treasurer, Robert Skidmore, regarding problem s with the banks in Lake County not being equipped to do
imaging. Mr. Allen proceeded to state that Cook County does receive the front image and corresponding
image of the PIN number to which payment was appl ied to, to help detect error or settle any dispute.
Commissioner Sutker stated that this is different than what he has heard and asked for something in
writing from Lake County referencing what Mr. Allen expressed. He asked what are the other problems?
Mr. Allen remarked in Lake County there are 200,000 PIN numbers and approximately 50 participating
banks, while in Cook County there are 1.5 million PIN numbers and 191 banks. He noted there are
col lateralization issues, where community banks are required to have certain leve ls of col lateral in order
to be taking in this money. The banks must show in excess of 100%.
Mr. Allen expressed that the lock box is an important first step in enhancing investment performance and
customer service. He indicated that RFPs were sent to 50 banks and I 2 responses were received and 11
banks declined to participate in this venture.
Commissioner Sutker asked why I I banks declined to participate?
Mr. Allen stated that the responses can be provided to the commissioners. For example, he expressed that
some banks were not ready, did not have the ability to handle such transactions or were transferring
technology and equipment at thi s time.
Commissioner Sutker was disturbed with the County Treasurer's Office brochure listing LaSalle National
Bank locations on the back. He stated there must be a way that the County can provide a service
conveniently to the county 's taxpayers which would include all federally insured banks that are equipped
and wil ling to participate in this program . The Treasurer's goal should be to include more federa lly
insured banks.

932

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Mr. Allen stated that the Treasurer's goal is to include all banks for more convenience and has even been
exploring currency exchanges, in the communities that have no community banks. A long term goal is to
allow taxpayers to pay on the internet. The Treasurer's Office wants to provide as many different options
as possible for the taxpayer.
Commi ssioner Sutker asked what is the interest that the County receives from LaSalle Bank on the
amount of money that is kept in the lockboxes during the period of time they retain the sums?
Mr. Allen commented that LaSalle National Bank was a key component in increasing interest earnings.
Peter Karahalios, Legal Counsel/First Deputy Treasurer, Treasurer' s Office, stated that the way the
accounts are structured is that the money goes from LaSalle Bank into a concentration account. The
concentration account is swept into a Repo Account, earning 200 basis points more than the NOW
account. The rate of return is approximately 5.2 to 5.3%.
Commissioner Sutker stated that LaSal le Bank acquires its profit from that amount above 5.2% which it
can generate using those dollars for investment.
Mr. Karahalios stated LaSalle Bank is making the amount that they are able to charge the County given
the number of PIN numbers that go through the lock box.
Commissioner Sutker stated the County should find a way to use this program as a spring board to a more
generic program to expand services. This program will let the banks compete with each other, w ith
respect to the services they provide to their customers. The Treasurer's brochure sends the wrong
message to the public, banks and taxpayers. The County should not look like it is favoring LaSalle
National Banks.
Comm issioner Lechowicz stated there was a memorandum distributed from Chairman Daley 's Office, to
the Commissioners. The memorandum originated from Treasurer Pappas and Grace Colbert of the
Budget Department as a correction on the Estimated Fiscal Impact for this item.
Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Comm issioner Sutker, moved to amend the Estimated Fiscal
Impact with respect to Item 233735, as follows: $360,000.00 $0.00. (Costs of this service is estimated at
$360,000.00 and will be offset through compensating balances through an interest bearing account).
Contract period : February I, 2000 through January 31, 200 I. (060 249 Aee0t1At).
Commissioner Hansen asked how the $500,000.00 and $360,000.00 figures relate on Item 233735?
Mr. Dauber responded that the $500,000.00 was put together for the budget. It was only an estimate;
what is needed is to complete the second installment transactions from the lockboxes to get a more
accurate number, to base the fi gures for year 2000. The way that this wi ll be paid is $360,000.00, but it
wi ll not be charged to an appropriation account. It will be charged to the "A Fund" Account.
Commissioner Hansen stated that the Treasurer's Office cannot obligate $360,000.00 to come from the A
Fund Account without the Board's approval. Ultimately, the County is paying this amount. He asked if it
can be zeroed-out?
Mr. Dauber indicated when the Treasurer's Office was goi ng through the budgetary process, it requested
that $500,000.00 be placed in the Appropriations Account 249. The Treasurer's Office was directed not
to do so and it was in the best interest of the County to leave it the way it was, paid outside of the C Fund
Account. He stated that it is paid out of the A Fund Account. The reason why the item is on the agenda
before the Board is to inform the Commissioners that the Treasurer's Office wi ll be handli ng it this way.
He noted the A Fund Account is not under the authority of the Board.

933

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Hansen asked if the State's Attorney' s Office could address the Committee on this issue
regarding Item 233735.
Kathy Howlett, Assistant State' s Attorney , responded that she would like to review this issue and will
respond in writing.
Commi ssioner Hansen voiced his concern, regarding whether the County is allowing a bank to charge
hidden fees.
Commissioner Lechowicz stated that the fi scal impact of thi s program is being shifted out of the taxing
portion of the budget to an interest bearing A Fund Account, and the Treasurer's Office is seeking the
Commissioner' s approval.
Commissioner Hansen stated that I 0% of all property tax revenue goes to Cook County and so I 0% of
the cost goes to the County as well. He stated if there is a $360,000.00 charge to be levied through
receiving less money then this is a cost passed on by the Treasurer' s Office. He asked what is the
statutory basis for this?
Mr. Dauber answered that the Treasurer' s Office does not believe it has sole authority over this issue.
The Treasurer' s Office did an RFP to comply with the Board ' s request. The A Fund Account does not
have an appropriation account fo r this to be charged to, however, there will be a cost incurred of
$360,000.00.
Commissioner Hansen expressed interest in all revenues generated by any and all funds in the Treasurer's
Office to the degree that those revenues are impacted by charges. He asked Tom G laser, Chief Financial
Officer, to address the committee as to where does the $360,000.00 expenditure appear in the County ' s
Budget?
Chairman Daley noted fo r the members, that the letter requesting an amendment to Item 233735 is also
signed by the Director of the Department of Budget & Management Services, Grace Colbert.
Mr. Glaser stated $360,000.00 is a cost estimate based on the volume of transactions processed by
LaSalle National Bank. It is a compensating balance.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the net figure? For example, if $720,000.00 is generated, the cost is
$360,000.00, the net revenue figure is $360,000.00. The request from the Treasurer' s Office cannot
reflect a fisca l impact of zero.

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Chief Financial
Officer submit a report to the committee, as far as the status of the funds. Included in the report
should be what is involved in the funds and which are approved and not approved by the Board. If
the funds are not approved, there should be an ordinance prepared by the Chief Financial Officer,
requesting that all funds be approved by this Board for any type of expenditures. The motion
carried.
Commissioner Lechowicz commented that this would alleviate Commissioner Hansen 's concern about
the A Fund possibly being spent w ithout Board authorization.
Commissioner Steele indicated there are communities within Cook County where LaSalle Bank has no
presence. Commissioner Steele hopes that other financial institutions are added to accommodate all
citizens in the next fiscal year.

934

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Hansen stated that good government finance practices should show gross revenues and
fees should be netted-out afterwards. Fees shown should be shown as they are paid by the Treasurer.
Commissioner Collins asked to look at all agencies that are not taxing bodies to ensure that no
departments have a fund that they can dip into at their discretion. She wants a report showing the source
of the funds to all departments.
Chairman Daley clarified that the request made by Commissioner Lechowicz will include all departments.
Commissioner Hansen stated concern of potentia l taxpayers s uits by charging a fee on collecting receipts.
There needs to be statutory authority. If there is a charge of$360,000 to collect $7 billion, there has to be
adequate authority.
Chairman Daley commented that Assistant State's Attorney Howlett wi ll guide the comm ittee on
Commissioner Hansen's concern.
Com missioner Silvestri asked what is the A Fund Account income over the last year?
Mr. Dauber answered $I 4, I 00,000.00 in interest earnings for Fiscal Year 1999.
Commissioner Si lvestri asked if the additional earnings were based on interest of deposits of tax
payments?
Mr. Dauber answered in the affirmative.
Commissioner Silvestri asked how much of the $14,100,000.00 earnings were spent?
Mr. Dauber answered that nothing was spent in Fiscal Year 1999. It was a budgetary item (060-249)
within the C Fund. The Treasurer's Office was directed to pay for this out of the interest income from the
A Fund Account in the Fiscal Year 2000 Budget. The $ 14. I million is a pass through. The $ 14. I million
went to the taxing bodies and agencies.
Commissioner S ilvestri commented that this item should not be used as an example. The committee has
seen items similar to th is originating from other offices. Often times, a fiscal impact of zero means this is
being paid out of some other source, even though it may not have an impact on the budget.
Commissioner Goslin indicated that a fiscal impact of zero would be misleading. There should be a
process open to all banks and e liminate the perceived favored status of LaSalle Banks. He pointed out
that hi s district borders 3 different counties where other banks work with various systems. He noted that
McHenry County will be opening a cyber account next year and perhaps that should be another avenue to
purs ue.
Commissioner Quigley echoed Commissioners Sutker's and Goslin's comments, to expand the program
to include additional banks. He stated the Treasurer's original request to place this item in the budget was
a better approach.
C hairman Daley asked Grace Colbert, Director of the Department of Budget and Management Services,
to address the Finance Committee.
Commissioner Lechowicz referenced a letter, ori ginating from Treasurer Pappas and Grace Colbert, as a
correction to the Estimated Fiscal Impact and inquired if Ms. Colbert agreed w ith the letter?

935

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Ms. Colbert agreed there is a zero estimated fi scal impact. She commented the historical practice has
been to administer the lock box through a compensating balance arrangement. There has never been a
disbursement or cost related to it.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked how much money is in the different accounts and do they come before
the County Board fo r approval of any type of expenditure?
Ms. Colbert stated that she could not answer the question because s he sees the budget only within the
context of the C Fund.
Commissioner Lechowicz commented that since this practice has been used in the past, does she have any
concerns regarding legal issues?
Ms. Colbert answered that a legal person should res pond to that question, however, this is a historical
practice.
Commissioner Hansen asked ifthe cost for this service had ever been in the budget?
Ms. Colbert responded in the negative to Commissioner Hansen's question, there is no cost as far as the
budget is concerned.
Comm issioner Hansen commented that there is a cost associated with this program, that th is is not a
minimum balance situation. Commi ssioner Hansen asked if the Board has been info rmed of the
mi nimum balance requirements and what it entails? He further asked if Ms. Colbert has been informed of
the composition of the minimum balance.
Ms. Colbert responded that she d id not know what the minimum balance requirements are and what
services are provided. This is outside the purview of the budget.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that this is a systematic problem. He said if the system needs reform, it
should be addressed as a whole.
Chairman Daley expressed caution in deferring Item 233735. He further stated that a precedent may be
set for all departments that present an item which reflects an estimated fiscal im pact of zero. Moreover,
the Budget Director has not onl y concurred with this matter, she also signed off on it.
Mr. Allen stated deferring the item will delay the program and it will become costly in terms of lost
interest earnings . A delay will cause the County to return to pre-lock box days. Commi ssioner Hansen
s uggested that Item 233735 be approved contingent upon receipt of the opini on from the State's
Attorney's Office.

Commissioner Ca rr, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to defer consideration of Item
233735. Following discussion, Commissioners Carr and Hansen withdrew their motion.
Chairman Da ley formally made the request to the State's Attorney 's Office for a legal opinion with
respect to Item 233735.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to approve Item 233735
contingent upon receipt of an opinion from the State's Attorney's Office. The motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Carr.

SECTION 4
Your Committee has considered the following communications from State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine
with reference to the industrial claims hereinafter mentioned.
Your Committee, therefore, recommends that the County Comptroller and County Treasurer be, and by
the adoption of this report, are authorized and directed to issue checks to the Industrial Commission to be
paid from the Workmen's Compensation Fund.
234225

JACQUELYN G. BUFORD, in the course of her employment as a Correctional Officer
sustained accidental injuries on September 20, 1997. The Petitioner slipped and fell, and as a
result she injured her left knee (bilateral ankle sprains, torn medial meniscus, left knee
requiring surgery). State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine, is submitting Industrial Commission
Lump Sum Petition and Order No. 98-WC-17693 in the amount of $15,000.00 and
recommends its payment. (Finance Subcommittee December 14, 1999).
Attorney:
Raymond P. Garza.

COMMISSIONER HANSEN VOTED PRESENT ON THE ABOVE ITEM.
234226

JACQUELINE FRANKLIN, in the course of her employment as a Transporter and then a
Typist at Cook County Hospital sustained accidental injuries on February 4, 1989 and May
27, 1994. The February 4, 1989 accident occurred when the Petitioner was transporting a
patient on a cart which moved sideways and in an attempt to straighten it out, she injured her
back (bulging discs at L4-L5; L5-S 1). The May 27, 1994 accident occurred when the
Petitioner slipped and fell, and as a result she injured her back (lumbosacral radiculopathy
with peripheral neuropathy). On November 19, 1999, the Industrial Commission modified
the Arbitrator' s decisions awarding the Petitioner a wage differential accrued and unpaid past
TTD benefits in the amount of $38,728.15 and $154.34 per week for the remainder of the
Petitioner's employment with the County. However, the Petitioner has agreed to accept
$35,000.00 for past due TTD and outstanding wage differential to avoid any further appeals.

983

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
In addition, the County wi ll still owe a wage differential as set out in the Illinois Industrial
Commission deci sion. The Finance Subcommittee on Industrial Claims approved these
decisions on February 8, 2000. The total amount due for past due wage differential and
unpaid TTD per the Illinois Industrial Commission decision is $35,000.00. The Illinois
Industrial Commission also ordered that the Petitioner, Jacqueline Franklin be paid a wage
differential of $ 154.34 per week to begin immediately. State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine,
is submitting Ind ustrial Commission Deci sion of Arbitrator, Award Nos. 89-WC-2696 1 and
94-WC-38032 in the amount of $35,000.00 and recommends its payment. (Finance
Subcommittee February 8, 2000). Attorney: Joel M. Bell, Law Firm ofTeplitz and Bell.
COMMISSIONER HANSEN VOTED PRESENT ON THE ABOVE ITEM.

1008

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Audit of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Tuesday, January 25, 2000 at the hour of 10:00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item(s) and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
Following the cal l of the meeting, Chairman Daley stated that questions had been submitted to various
departments and e lected officials on the agenda items. The Chairman requested copies of the responses
and questions be submitted to the Secretary to the Board and placed in the record as submitted to the
Comm ittee's report. Chairman Daley then recogni zed Commissioner Hansen.
On a matter of old business, Commissioner Hansen asked if the Chairman had received any
communication from Arthur Andersen or the Treasurer regarding the status of the Treasurer's Office turnover audit report for the year ending November 30, 1998, by Arthur Andersen. Commissioner Hansen
stated he believed the Treasurer had given the Board a target date of Friday, January 21 , 2000 for the
report to be distributed to the Members. Chairman Daley stated he believed the President's Office had
received some type of communication on the issue and called on Tom Glaser to respond on behalf of the
Administration.
Tom Glaser stated that the turn-over audit report was in the process of being completed by Arthur
Andersen. He confirmed that a letter, dated January 13, 2000, from Arthur Andersen to President Stroger
was recei ved and did request assistance in obtaining tax distribution information from the MIS
department. This information is necessary in order to complete the turnover audit report.
Commissioner Hansen asked if there was a response on this matter from the Treas urer's Office regarding
the reason for the delay of the report. The Chair called on Kim Feeney, a representati ve of the
Treasurer's Office, to respond.
Kim Feeney stated the Treasurer' s report had not been forwarded to the Members due to the fact that two
important items needed for the com pletion of the audit have not yet been received. Ms. Feeney cited the
two items as: I) the dummy distribution information from MIS, which allows the Treasurer's Office to
know if there are any items that still need to be distributed or redistri buted to the taxing districts; and 2)
information from the State of Illinois, which Arthur Andersen is working on regard ing monies that could
have been improperly escheated to the State in the past.
Ms. Feeney explained that at the time the Treasurer provided a target date for transmitting the report to
the Board, she had not been informed of any reason for delay and was unaware that Arthur Andersen was
still awaiting the above referenced items and could not com plete the report without the information.
Ms. Feeney stated that she would immediately relay to the Treasurer the Members concerns.
The Chairman then proceeded to the first item on the agenda.
I.

C lerk of the Circuit Court - Child Support Enforcement Division, Financial Report for the year
ended November 30, 1997, by Laura A. Burman, County Auditor.

Deferred at the October 26, 1999 meeting.

1009

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Referring to a letter, dated October 29, 1999, from Heather Crossley to Commi ssioner Hansen
recommending investing in an automated billing system to a llow the county to improve the tracking and
collection of the admi nistrative fees added on to child s upport payments, Commissioner Lechowicz asked
if the automated billing system had been implemented or whether there was a better tracking method in
place for the admi nistrative fee collections. The C hair called on George Rada, a representative of the
C lerk of the C ircuit Court's Office, to respond.
George Rada stated the Circuit Court Clerk's Office does not have an automated billing system, but has
implemented the Auditor's recommendations, in terms of developing and maintaining internal written
policies and collection proced ures. He explained that the offi ce sends out three billing notices, wh ich
references the statutory req ui rements to the obligors, in an attempt to collect the child support
administrative fee. Mr. Rada stated when those letters are neglected, the Circuit Court Clerk's Office
consults with and re lies on the State's Attorney' s Office for enforcement of the collections.
In response to Commissioner Lechowicz's question, regarding why the office had not yet implemented an
automated billing system and the reason for the delay in resolving this matter since thirteen million
dollars in uncollected administrative fees date back to January of 1996, George Rada stated the C ircuit
Court Clerk' s Office did contact the State's Attorney ' s Offi ce as recommended by the Auditor to
determine the best action to take and is awaiting a res ponse on what recourse the office has in terms of
collecting the past years delinquent fees as well as what can be done to enforce the payment of future
collections.
Mr. Rada stated the office has consulted with Pat Dri scoll from the State's Attorney's Office and is
awaiting a response on whether to pursue an automated billing system, a private collection agency,
e nforcement through the State's Attorney ' s Office, and/or a change in the statutory authority to allow the
administrative fee to be court ordered. Mr. Rada noted that the office is anxious to resolve the collection
problem and is waiting to review the State' s Attorney ' s recommendations.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked if Mr. Rada could confirm if there was a person from the State' s
Attorney' s Civil Division assigned to enfo rce the administrative fee. Mr. Rada stated that he believed
there was but no enforcement has been pursued.
On that iss ue, the Chair called on a representative from the State' s Attorney to respond to the question of
what is be ing done to pursue the past years delinquent fees collection and future enforcement of the
county's child support administrative fees.
James Michael Bailey, Assistant State 's Attorney in the Civil Actions Bureau, presented himself to the
members as the indi vidual in the State 's Attorney ' s Office asked to review the coll ection and enforcement
of the county ' s child support administrative fees. Mr. Bailey informed the members that there are two
distinct and separate statutes that permit two separate $36 dollar child s upport administrative and
maintenance fees (citing 750 ILCS 5/7 11 and 705 ILCS 5/27.2.) Mr. Bailey said he needed clarification
from the Auditor regarding which statute the audit re port is referencing when it cites House Bill 277. Mr.
Bailey explained the fee authorized under 750 I LCS 5/7 11 is intended for the county ' s use and stated it
specifies that the court shall order the payor making payments directly to the clerk to pay the clerk a fee at
the rate of $3.00 per month for every month in w hich the chi Id support payment is due and the fee is to be
made semi-annually (on the January i s• and July l " payments) and shall be held in a separate fund by the
Circuit Court Clerk and the contents of which sha ll be paid over to the county treasury, on a monthly
basis or at such period as the county Treasurer shall determine, to re imburse the county for the cost of
ma inta ining the child support enforcement program.

10 10

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Mr. Bailey assumed the confusion involved in the collection of fee authorized under 750 ILCS may be
due to the fact that the Circuit Court Clerk has sought to collect and has asked the State's Attorney to
enforce an administrative fee pursuant to 705 ILCS 105/27.2bb(4). He explained that he has discussed
this matter with individuals in the Circuit Court Clerk's Office and has tried to explain that the fee they
wish to collect under this section of the law is unenforceable. Mr. Bailey noted that this statute only
allows for a permissive fee to be collected by the Clerk that must remain separate and apart from the court
orders and therefore makes it very difficult to enforce. He explained that under 705 ILCS 105/27.2,
subsection bb-4, the Circuit Court Clerk, if authorized by the County Board, may collect an annual fee up
to $36 dollars that shall be in addition to and separate from amounts ordered to be paid as maintenance or
child support and shall be deposited into a separate maintenance child support collection fund of which
the Circuit Court Clerk shall be the custodian, ex-officio, and is intended to be used by the Circuit Court
Clerk to further maintenance and child support. It also specifies that the Clerk may recover an additional
cost incurred in the collection of the annual fee.
Commissioner Lechowicz requested a written response from the State's Attorney as to recommendations
to the Audit committee on how to implement the collection and enforcement of the adm inistrative and
maintenance of chi ld support collection fees.
Jn response to Commissioner Hansen's question, regarding the reason for the high volume of money
being held in the Imprest Bank account, George Rada stated that this amount represents checks or monies
that have been disbursed but were returned to the Clerk's office or not cashed by financial institutions.
Commissioner Hansen asked what the aging was on that account's outstandi ng balance. Mr. Rada stated
that some checks go back to 1991.
Commissioner Hansen requested a year-by-year aging schedule of the outstanding check balance in the
Imprest Bank Account and a legal opinion on the county's obligation to escheat this money.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's question, regarding if the county has an escheatment problem
related to this acco unt, George Rada stated that the office is looking into the escheatment issue as it
relates to money attached to pending cases and checks returned by the Illinois Department of Financial
Institutions requesting additional information.
Comm issioner Hansen asked the Auditor, if the county was allowed to hold monies for a length of time
over eight years, or is the county required to escheat the monies to the lllinois Department of Financial
Institutions after a certain number of years. Laura Burman stated that generally escheatments are made on
money held for over seven years. However in regards to money the office reported was returned by the
State, there may be a different protocol the State follows relating to pending cases.
In response to Commissioner Hansen 's question on the status of retrieving information on checks
returned to the office due to a lack of information or an invalid address, George Rada stated that the office
is in the process of improving its procedure used to locate case infonnation as well as to update payees
information when the payment notices are returned due to the obligor moving and not supplying the office
with a forwarding address. In such cases, he noted, the information is not on ly important in the collection
of delinquent county fees, but usually involves non-custodial parents who are also delinquent in their
child support payments to the custodial parent. Mr. Rada stated that the Circuit Court Clerk's Office has
hired an outside consultant to provide the necessary matching record equipment to assist the office with
this new match report system.
Commissioner Hansen requested a written response from the Circuit Court Clerk regarding a target date
for completing the match report and updating the clerk's records system.

1011

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
On a separate issue involving child support, Commissioner Hansen stated that he recently had read that
custodial parents receive an inadeq uate share of the total dollars collected on child support payments
ordered.
Commissioner Hansen requested a report on what share of child support dollars ordered in Cook County
goes to the custodial parent. Commissioner Hansen asked that the committee review the level of support
infonnation at its next meeting and examine the relative success or failure of the child support system.

Commissioner Hansen moved to defer Item 1 to the next meeting of the committee. Seconded by
Commissioner Lechowicz, the motion carried and the item was deferred.
Chairman Daley requested that during the period of deferral the Circuit Court Clerk's Office and
State's Attorney's Office get together with the Auditor in order to complete all requests for
information and to prepare a recommendation on the child support fee collection and enforcement
issue for review by the Audit committee and the full Board.
