23209 1

BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVlCES, by Ruth M. Rothstein, Chief, transmitting a
Communication, dated September 16, 1999:
This letter is to formally request that the Bureau of Health Services Audited Financial
Statements, related Management Letter, and request for Bad Debt write-off for fi scal year
+998 1995 and prior years be forwarded to the Audit Committee of the Board of
Commissioners for discussion.

Referred to the Audit Committee on November 9, 1999.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's question regardi ng a statement on page I-Appendi x A, and the
status of the recommendation to increase the $250 purchasing limit, Tom Glaser stated that he had briefed
the President on several options and will come back to the Board with a recommendation on the iss ue.
In response to Commi ssioner Hansen's question, on page 3-Appendix A, regarding an explanation of
what a charge master and charge structure is, Alvin Holley stated that the charge master is simply the
table used fo r different fees that refers to over I 0,000 line items in the charge structure. Mr. Holley noted
that these charges typically relate to various radiology and lab fees and stated that in order to increase
these fees and provide a more detailed report of each fee the charge master needs to be updated.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's questi on regarding a tim e frame for completing the
recommendation, Alvin Holley stated that the Bureau has completed its solicitation for bid proposals and
wou ld be submitting a recommendation on a vendor very soon.
In response to Commissioner Hansen·s question, on page 3, regarding where the aging sched ule was for
the $880 million uncollectable account, the Auditor stated that she had passed this request onto Alvin
Holley along with the other questions she had received from the Commissioner only yesterday. Laura
Bumian stated that the Bureau's responses and request for additional information would be provided to
Commissioner Hansen.
Commissioner Hansen requested information in writing from Alvin Holley regarding the aging schedule
for the $880 million uncollectable debt figure, including the amount associated with each year up to fiscal
year 1998.

101 2

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Hansen expressed some concern regarding why $880 mi ll ion in uncollectable debt had not
been cleaned up earl ier, as permitted under the Bad Debt Write-Off Policy. Laura Burman stated that th is
was the first annual write-off since the adoption of the policy by this Body. She pointed out that the
communication before the committee today includes a separate schedule item referred to as the
"Summary of Bad Debt Write-Off for fiscal year 1995 and prior." Ms. Burman noted that the schedule
did not include fiscal years 1996, 1997 and 1998, since collections for these years had not yet been
completed. She stated the Bureau of Health Services was requesting approval of the bad debt write-off
schedule for fiscal year 1995 and prior years. She also noted that from this point forward the committee
would be considering bad debt write-off on an annual basis.
In response to Vice Chairman Gosli n's question regarding a more specific defin ition of the term " prior
years" as used in the summary, A lvi n Holley stated that prior years refers to fiscal year 1994.
Vice Chairman Goslin requested a written copy of the Bad Debt Write-Off Policy approved by this Body
from the Auditor.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's question regarding if the $880 million uncollectable figure
includes the bad debt for fiscal years 1994 and 1995, Laura Burman stated that it did.
In response to Commissioner Hansen' s question, on page 5, regardi ng an explanation for the contributed
capital depreciation of $ 19 million, Alvin Holley explained there is certain property in assets that the
county purchased with bond issues. He said the Bureau records such property as fi xed assets and records
the offset as contributed capital. Mr. Holley explained that after the Bureau depreciates that asset, the
contributing capital must be reduced to allow it to be fairly stated and not run against the operating fund.
Mr. Holley stated that the operating fund reflected is strictly for presentation.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's question to the Chief Financial Officer of the County regarding
when the county instituted this depreciation policy, Tom Glaser stated that the hospital is required to
depreciate assets in order to do the federal report used to receive Medicare/ Medicaid reimbursement. Mr.
Glaser stated the county had not yet instituted a depreciation policy; however, the hospital did institute a
policy on depreciation.
Commissioner Hansen stated this was the first time he had heard of the hospital's depreciation policy and
noted his concern that the County Board had not approved it. Alvin Holley responded that the hospital's
books are recorded on an accrual basis and with the accrual financial statement you must use
depreciation. Mr. Holley stated that the depreciation guidelines used by the county's hospitals come from
the American Hospital Association, which includes suggested depreciable usefu l life that most hospitals
use in the United States.
Commissioner Hansen requested from the Bureau of Health Services a copy of the depreciation policy
used by the hospital.
In response to Commissioner Hansen 's question regarding an explanation for the deficiency figure of
revenue over expenses showing $38 million, Alvin Holley stated that thi s figu re reflects the bottom line
and is derived from subtracting the $333 million non-operating revenue from the $37 1 million loss from
operations.
Commissioner Lechowicz requested a synopsis of past and current bad debt write-offs, along with a
schedule of future bad debt write-offs for fi scal years 1996, 1997 and 1998. Commissioner Hansen
requested that a percentage or estimate for fisca l year 1999 be inc luded in this information.

Reason:

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON LEGISLATION
AND INTERGOVERNMENTAL RELATIONS
February I 8, 2000
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Hansen, Vice-Chair Lechowicz, Commissioners Daley, Sims, Sutker (5)

Absent:

Commissioners Collins, Moran, Schumann, and Silvestri (4)

Also Present:

Commissioner Butler (I); Steve Morrill - Cook County Board's representative in
Springfield; Eugene Barnes - Cook County President's Office representative in
Springfield; Terry Steczo - Deputy Assessor for Administration and Intergovernmental
Relations, Cook County Assessor's Office; Sue Sikes - Legislative Liai son, Cook County
Assessor's Office; Gary Rycyzyn - Director of Elections, Cook County Clerk's Office;
Gerry Reyes - Legislative Director, Cook County State's Attorney's Office; Ed Carik Director of Intergovernmental Affairs, Cook County Sheriff's Office; John Potts representative, Cook County Board of Review; Michael Kasper - representative, Cook
County Recorder of Deeds; Peter Coffey - Director of Governmental Affairs, Chicago
Botanic Garden; Martha Benaroya - Chicago Zoological Society ; Caryn Stancik and Carl
McConnick - Cook County Forest Preserve; Debra Stone - Intergovernmental
Coordinator, Cook County President's Office; and Sandra Overberg - Legislative
Coordinator, Cook County Board

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County met purs uant to notice on Friday, February 18, 2000, at the hour of I 0:00 A.M., in the Board
Room, Room 569, County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Chai rman Hansen stated the purpose of the meeting was to review the Year 2000 legislative program for
each agency of Cook County government, to include the Forest Preserve, the Chicago Botanic Garden,
and the Zoological Society. The Chairman then recognized various representatives from the county
elected offices and agencies.
Chairman Hansen proceeded to discussion of the first item on the agenda.
I. HB 4698 - Public Defender Immunity Act
Vice Chairman Lechowicz urged support of the bill because it would ensure a protection in the courts for
employees in the Public Defender's Office. A recent court ruling removes their immunity thereby
opening employees up to being s ued and increasing the county's liability.

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to support House Bill 4698. Seconded by Commissioner Sutker,
the motion carried.

1021

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
2. SB 1303 - Property Taxes: Objections in Court
Steve Morrill informed the members that Senate Bill 1303 was on third reading in the Senate. He stated
the proposal would allow a ll taxing bodies to intervene in any tax objection case and represent
themselves, thereby relieving the State's Attorney of this duty. Vice Chairman Lechowicz stated concern
with removing the current juri sdiction held by the State's Attorney.
Chairman Hansen called on Gerry Reyes to address any concerns the State's Attorney's office might have
regarding the bill.
Gerry Reyes stated the office had some technical questions regarding how objection procedures wou ld be
implemented. He a lso commented the office was rev iewing the impact on tax objection cases if the
State's Attorney was relieved of hi s duties in such cases. Mr. Reyes noted that a similar proposal was
introduced last year but never made it out of the Rules Committee.
Vice Chairman Lechowicz asked if the Cook County State's Attorney's office opposes Senate Bill 1303.
Gerry Reyes stated the office did not take a formal position on the bill but had opposed it in the past.
Commissioner Sutker suggested that the county's lobbyists request an amendment deleting the text
stating, "the State's Attorney shall be relieved of the defense" and inserting the language, "the State's
Attorney may join in the defense."
Commissioner Sutker asked whether his suggested amendatory language had ever been di scussed or
proposed in the past. In response, Gerry Reyes stated that to date no amendatory language has been
proposed.
In response to Commissioner Daley's question regarding the vote in committee on Senate Bill 1303, Steve
Morrill stated he did not believe there were any objections to the measures in committee. Commissioner
Daley asked if the county took a position on the bill. Steve Morrill stated that the county took no
position.
Commissioner Daley asked if when an elected county official opposes a measure does the county do the
same, Steve Morrill stated that pos itions are only taken when this Body and the Board approve a position.
Commissioner Daley commented on the need for the county to take a position on bills during hearings in
substantive committees. Vice Chairman Lechowicz agreed and stated there needs to be a coordinated
effort by the entire county on al l legislation.
Commissioner Sims asked for information in regards to any action taken on the bill.
Sandra Overberg confirmed that no formal opposition was filed on behalf of the Board or the
Administration in committee.

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to oppose Senate Bill 1303. Seconded by Commissioner Daley,
the motion carried.
3. SB 1276 - Property Taxes: Attorneys before Board of Review
Steve Morri ll stated that Senate Bill 1276 passed, without objection this week, out of the Senate Revenue
Committee and is on second reading on the Senate floor. Mr. Morrill stated the proposal would provide,
in Cook County only, that non-attorneys are authorized to represent taxpayers before the Cook County
Board of Review.

1022

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
C ha irman Hansen called on the representative of the Board of Review, John Potts, to comment on the bill.
Mr. Potts informed the members that the Board of Review opposed the bill in committee, along with the
Illinois State Bar Association's (ISBA) Real Estate Tax Division. He stated testimony was given
addressing the Board's and ISBA's concerns, but the bill passed out of Senate Revenue this week by a
vote of9 yeas, 2 nays. Mr. Potts stated that currently a roll call of the Senate members is being conducted
and the bill is expected to come up for a vote next week.
In response to Chairman Hansen's question regarding if all three Commissioners on the Cook County
Board of Review opposed Senate Bill 1276, John Potts stated that they did.

Hearing no motion from the members of the committee, the Chair ruled that Item 3, Senate Bill
1276, be deferred.
4. SB 1546 - Property Taxes: Assessment Notices

Noting the committee had been informed earlier that Item 4 was presumably dead, but made aware
that bill could be resurrected in amendatory form, the Chair ruled that Item 4, Senate Bill 1546, be
deferred.
5. SB 1645 - Property Taxes: Mortgage Lender Notices
Steve Morrill stated that Senate Bill 1645 passed out of the Senate Revenue Committee th is week and was
on second reading on the Senate floor. He stated that the proposal would provide, in Cook County only, that
when an assessment increase notice is mailed by the Assessor's office to a mortgage lender, within 5 days of
receipt, the mortgage lender shall mail a copy of the notice to each owner or mortgagor of the property.
Eugene Barnes informed the members that Senate Bill 1645 is an initiative of Assessor Houlihan.

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to support Senate Bill 1546. Seconded by Commissioner Daley,
the motion carried.
6. HB 2976 - FOIA: Litigation Records
Steve Morrill stated that House Bill 2976 fai led in comm ittee and is technically "dead" for the session.

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to oppose House Bill 2976 and similar provisions that may arise
in the future. Seconded by Commissioner Sutker, the motion carried.
7. H B 113 7 - Elections: Local Primaries
Steve Morrill stated that House Bill 113 7 is currently on the Secretary's desk in the Senate on nonconcurrence and will be subject to a conference commi ttee report. Mr. Morrill informed the commi ttee
that the proposed conference committee report's language is intended to amend the Election Code to allow
new voting equipment (purchased by Cook County and the Chicago Board of Elections) to be used as
intended. Mr. Morrill stated that changes to the Code would allow the voter to directly insert the ballot
into the machine rather than handing it to the e lection judge and the machine would automatically tally
voti ng cards.

1023

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Daley asked to hear from Gary Rycyzyn, Director of Elections, Cook County Clerk's
Office. Gary Rycyzy n stated that he had not seen the amendment to House Bill 11 37 but noted that if the
proposal contains changes to the Election Code to allow new voting equipment to be used as approved by
the County Board, he would recommend support.
In response to Chairman Hansen's question regard ing whether the county's election process would be
disrupted if this legislation was not adopted, Gary Rycyzyn stated there would be no disruption. He
explained that the election authorities could still use the new equipment, but with the old election
procedure.
In response to Commissioner Daley's question if the new machines would allow for the rejection of ballot
cards not signed by an election judge, Gary Rycyzyn noted that the election authorities were requested not
to use this feature during the test period.
Steve Morrill further stated that the reason this feature is not being used during the test is due to concerns
relating to ballot security.
Commissioner Daley asked if the issue relating to over-counts was still in the proposal, Steve Morrill
responded that it was not.
Commissioner Daley stated that House Bill 11 37 appears to lack two primary features the County Board
was concerned with when it approved the purchase of the new equipment.
Chairman Hansen asked Gary Rycyzyn if the ballot card does not contain an election judge' s initials,
during the test period, would the ballot be rejected. Gary Rycyzyn stated the equipment does not
currently carry this feature.
Commissioner Sutker stated he was very disturbed at thi s since the board was informed that the pilot
program would include the two features mentioned. He noted the pilot program will accomplish nothing
in terms of testing the intended uses of the new equipment.
Chairman Hansen commented that he was disturbed that the Chairman and committee were not being
full y briefed by lobbyists and representati ves from the elected offices on changes being made by this draft
legislation impacting the county.

Commissioner Sutker moved to defer House Bill 1137. Seconded by Vice C hairman Lechowicz, the
motion carried.
8. SB 1890 - Elections: Absentee Voting

After hearing that the bill had failed to advance to the Senate floor by the February 17, 2000
committee deadline, Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to oppose Senate Bill 1890 or any similar
provisions that may arise in the future. Seconded by Commissioner Sutker, the motion carried.
9. HB 3036 - Senior Citi zen Prescription Drug Program Act

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to support House Bill 3036. Seconded by Commissioner Daley,
the motion carried.

1024

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
10. HB 3225 - Counties Code: Sheriffs Merit Board
Eugene Barnes stated that House Bill 3225 was amended the day before in committee to remove language
opposed by the Administration calling for merit board members to receive any wage adjustments
approved by the board for its employees. Mr. Barnes stated that upon adoption of the amendment, the
Administration removed its opposition.
Chairman Hansen stated concern in not receiving any oral or written justification from the Sheriffs Office
on the need for two additional merit board members. He noted also that the membership of the current
Board was at odds with the statue copy provided to the committee.
Ed Carik assured the Members that the changes in the statute, in regards to the Board's salaries and
membership, are permissive since the statute states that each requires the consent and approval of the
County Board.
In response to Commissioner Sutker's question on whether the party affiliation of the Board changes
proportionately with the increase in membership, Ed Carik stated that the statute' s current provisions on
party membership would not change.

Commissioner Daley moved to support House Bill 3225, as amended. Seconded by Vice Chairman
Lechowicz, the motion carried.
Chairman Hansen and Commissioner Sutker voted Present on this item.
11 . SB 1522 - Counties Code: Cell Tower Guidelines

Steve Morrill stated that Senate Bill 1522 is a Metro Counties initiative. He stated that the
telecommunication carriers oppose the discretionary provisions being made mandatory. Mr. Morrill
suggested that Sandra Overberg might have some information on this issue.
Sandra Overberg stated that at the last Metro Counties Association meeting, the bill was mentioned as a
priority initiative of Lake County, which the association supported. She stated that the intent of the bill is
to allow local authorities to protect residential communities and property owners. Ms. Overberg stated
that Cook County has taken a neutral position in the past since zoning and building authority is not
restricted under the statute for home rule bodies.
Vice Chairman Lechowicz requested that a copy of Senate Bill 1522 be sent to the Building and Zoning
Department asking for a written response regarding any impact the bill might have on Cook County.

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to defer Senate Bill 1522. Seconded by Commissioner Sutker, the
motion carried.
12. HB 4651 - Employee Wage Deductions for Debt Collection
Chairman Hansen recognized Carl McCormick to make any observation on the bill as it relates to Cook
County Forest Preserve District employees.
Carl McCormick stated that the District had no problems with the provisions and is in favor of House Bill
4651.

1025

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to support House Bill 4651. Seconded by Commissioner Daley,
the motion carried.
Commissioner Daley moved to include the budget memo from Debra Stone into the record.
Seconded Commissioner Sutker, the motion carried.
Vice Chairman Lechowicz moved to include the memos from the Office of the Clerk of the Circuit
Court and the Office of the Assessor into the record. Seconded by Commissioner Daley, the motion
carried. (The referenced documents are on file in the Office of the County C lerk.)
Commissioner Daley moved to adjourn. Seconded by Commissioner Sims, the motion carried and
the meeting was adjourned.

VILLAGE OF GLENVIEW (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Comm unication,
dated October 4, I 999 from Deborah Sims, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee,
submitting a request from Robbins, Salomon & Patt, Ltd., Attorneys at Law:
Re:

Village of Glenview No-Cash Bid Application for PINS: 04-3 5- I 06-034 and 04-32200-044

We represent the Village of G lenview, which is requesting the assistance of Cook County in
making a no cash bid to acquire two separate properties located within the municipal
boundaries of the Village. The properties are identified by PIN 04-35- I 06-034 (Vol. I 34)
and PIN 04-32-200-044 (Vol. I 34). The properties to be acquired have been tax delinquent
for each of two or more years. After acquiring the property bearing PIN 04-35-1 06-034, the
Vil lage intends to return the property to the tax rolls by conveying it to a developer for a
multi-family residential development. With regard to the property bearing PIN 04-32-200044, the Village wi ll continue to utilize this property as a detention bas in as part of the
Village's storm water management program.
Included with this request are:

*

*
*
*

Certified copies of Resolutions for each PIN fo rmally requesting the bid;
Current title search for each property;
Sidwell maps for each PIN.
Two photographs of each property.

As the attorneys for the Village we will obtain the tax deeds and the Village will bear al l legal
and other costs associated with the acq uisition of these properties.
Troy Deckert, Department of Planning & Development, stated the Village of Glenview is interested in the
first parcel which contains a storm water pond, and a private developer plans to build a multi-family unit
on the second parcel. Approval of the request will allow the Village to clear back taxes and return the
property to the tax rolls.
Commissioner Collins asked if the Village will acquire the property and clear the back taxes for a private
developer?
Mr. Deckert responded that a developer is building a condominium multi-family building. He stated the
taxes will be cleared so that the developer can develop the area.
Commissioner Collins asked if this is standard procedure?
Mr. Deckert responded the No-Cash Bid process will extinguish all cash liens.
Randy Kemmerer, Assistant State' s Attorney, stated the No-Cash Bid is a payment of taxes. The Village
of Glenview wi ll cancel the certificate that will be payment in full and the taxes are extinguished by
satisfying the tax liens. He commented this process has been approved before on behalf of the Village of
Dixmor. Mr. Kemmerer stated that is an over-the-counter sale and the legal effect is to pay the taxes even
though no dollars change hands.

1027

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Commissioner Butler stated the property is given to the municipality and the municipality gives the
property to the developer who will develop it and put it back on the tax rolls.
Commissioner Carr concurred with Commissioner Butler and commented that this is a win-win situation
for the County because the property will be put back on the tax rolls.

Commissioner Goslin moved approval of Item 231596, seconded by Commissioner Butler, the
motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTIONS

OO-R-138
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT AND GREGG GOSLIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, CARL R. HANSEN, TED .L ECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Cook County is home to more than 67,000 acres of unique ly diverse open space consisting
of prairies, savannas, wetlands, and forests unparalleled by any other urban setting; and
WHEREAS, the beauty of our natura l landscape is often overshadowed by an urban setting; and
WHEREAS, lllinois is known as the Prairie State; and
WHEREAS, prior to settlement, much of Cook County was prairie and savanna; and
WHEREAS, Echinacea, commonly known as Purple Coneflower, is a beautiful and prominent example
of our native prairie ecosystem; and
WHEREAS, the planting of Purple Coneflower in an urban setting provides an appropriate reminder of
our natural landscape.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED the Cook County Board of Commissioners hereby names the
Purple Coneflower the official Cook County flower on this ninth day of March, in the year 2000.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that this Resolution be made part of the official proceedings of the Board
of Commissioners of Cook County.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of March 2000.

WHEREAS, Almighty God, in his infinite wisdom, has called Jeanne Simon, wife of former U.S. Senator
Paul Simon, from our midst; and
WHEREAS, widely respected for her energy, integrity and gift for bridging divisions, Jeanne was far
more than a supportive wife; she was a former state representative who relinquished her General
Assembly seat after two terms in 1960 to marry her husband; and
WHEREAS, regarded as a trailblazer, Jeanne Simon was one of the first female law students at
Northwestern University and one of the first women in the General Assembly; and
WHEREAS, after completing law school, Jeanne accepted a position as an assistant Cook County state's
attorney, and was elected to the lllinois General Assembly; and
WHEREAS, as one of the first female legislators, Jeanne Simon devoted her energy toward promoting
literacy programs and funding for libraries; and
WHEREAS, with the passing of Jeanne Simon, we have lost a genuine pioneer--a well respected state
representative, author and devoted wife who worked relentlessly to improve the quality of education and
libraries across the nation; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of
the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby express its deepest condolences and
most heartfelt sympathy to the many friends and loved ones of Jeanne Simon; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of Jeanne
Simon, so that her memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His Infinite Wisdom has called from our midst,
HOWARD LEIBOVITZ
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was the loving husband of Carol, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was the dear brother of Myron (Myrna) and Calvin (Elaine), and

1037

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was the affectionate uncle of Lynn (Paul), Alan (Julie) Gary, Larry
(Liz), Marc (Debbie) and Amie, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was the adoring great uncle of Alli son, Tori, Katy, Jonathan, Sam,
Amanda, Ky le and Michael, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was the cherished son-in-law of Lee Lofberg, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz was an inventor and businessman. He co-founded a manufacturing
business, now Paratech, Inc., when he was 20 years old with Peter Nielson and Robert Benker. The
business produced emergency service and heavy-duty rescue equipment, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz's business partner, Peter Nielson stated, "Two out of three of us got
started in business before we were old enough to sign the papers" , and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz's interest in emergency service equipment was piqued when he
volunteered for the fire and rescue service, a civil defense adjunct of the Chicago Fire Department, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz attended the Illinois Institute of Technology. He built some equipment
during his stint with the service and decided to start a business with Peter Nielson and Robert Benker, and
WHEREAS, the men "scratched together a few hundred dollars" and opened a store on North Clark
Street in 1960, where they invented the "K-12" saw, which became an important tool in fighting fires and
is still in production. The tool enabled firefighters to cut open roofs of buildings in minutes, venting
smoke and heat so firefighters below could enter the building, and
WHEREAS, the business later moved to Fulton Street in Chicago before permanently relocating to south
suburban Frankfort in 1974. The company branched into other emergency equipment, designing rescue
vehicles and forcible entry tools for emergency crews and the military, and
WHEREAS, Howard Leibovitz's brother, Myron stated, "This equipment saved a lot of Jives all over
the world." He personally held five design patents. Peter Nielson described Howard as, "A born
inventor. .. he was extremely technically qualified and a brilliant guy", and
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby offer
its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family of Howard Leibovitz and joins them in
their sorrow at this time of loss, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body and that a suitable copy of same be tendered to the family of Howard Leibovitz.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of March 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

practice, he was the Chairman of TC Manufacturing Company, and
WHEREAS, Herbert Stern, Jr. was active in numerous charitable and civic organizations including the

growing Polish community;
WHEREAS, the Sisters immediately set to work at St. Mary of the Angels Parish in Chicago,
where 400 pupils awaited their teaching;
WHEREAS, the Sisters spread their ministry to other paris hes rapidly as Chicago' s immigrant
population multiplied ;

1041

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

Resurrection Academy, an elementary and boarding school for girls;
WHEREAS, in 1920, the Congregation bought a second parcel of land along Talcott A venue
where Res urrection Medical Center exists today, the first hospital in what is Chicago's largest
Catholic health care system;
WHEREAS, in 1953 the Sisters opened Resurrection Hospital, where their ministry operates
both as a public community resource and as a source of comfort, care and inspiration on an
individual level ;
WHEREAS, in add ition to Resurrection Health Care, which includes four major hospitals and
over 60 sites of care, the Sisters run a day care center in Chicago, the Provincial Home, a home
for senior sisters, and Resurrection High School for girls, which U.S. News & World Report
ranked as one of the top high schools in the country;
WHEREAS, across the country, the Si sters teach in elementary and secondary schools and
operate nurseries, nursing homes and childcare centers; and
WHEREAS, the Sisters provide spiritual counseling to unwed mothers, the severely disabled, the
elderly, the poor, the lone ly, and the ill , helping them transform the occasions of life from loss to
gain, from despair to hope and from sadness to joy.

does hereby commemorate the Sisters of the Resurrection for 100 years of service; and
BE JT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of th is Resolution be spread upon the
official proceedings of this Honorable Body and that a copy of same be tendered to the Sisters of
the Resurrection in recognition of their 1OOth Anniversary in the United States.

OO-R-154
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, Harriet Tubman was born on the Eastern Shore of Maryland around 1820, and
escaped from slavery in I 849 making her way north by the Underground Railroad, an elaborate secret
network of safe houses organized for that purpose. She became one of the " railroad's" most active
conductors; and
WHEREAS, Harriet Tubman returned to the south time and time again leading more than 300
slaves to freedom, despite a sentence of death by torture, and huge rewards offered for her capture; and

1049

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000

WHEREAS, Harriet Tubman served with distinction as a nurse, laundress, and spy with the
Federal forces along the coast of South Carolina during the Civil War, she recei ved a government pension
30 years after the war as recognition of her work for the Federal Army; and
WHEREAS, Harri et Tubman provided an inspiration of liberty, justice and opportunity that
serves us still. She was a warrior in the battle for equality; now
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commi ssioners urge its'
citizens to pause and reflect upon the achievements of this remarkable woman joining communities across
the nation in commemorating March I 0, 2000, as Harriet Tubman Day; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this Resolution be spread upon the official record of this
Honorable Body and a suitable copy tendered to The Harriet Tubman Society of Stone Mountain, GA.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of March 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

contributions to others, and

WHEREAS Kathleen T. Kubey has dedicated much of her professional vocational life to caring for

devices at rest areas along the Illinois Interstate Highway system, provided free TTY's for the families of

convention highlighting the accomplishment of the deaf community, and

Award for distinguished contributions, and
WHEREAS Kathleen T. Ku bey has worked tirelessly on behalf of deaf/hearing impaired individuals and
their families to address their special needs, and has been an aggressive and determined advocate for the
interests of the deaf community, and
WHEREAS Kathleen T. Kubey began her remarkable career by teaching elementary classes to deaf
children, and soon became well known and highly regarded for her special rapport with youngsters, and

OO-R-169
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE EARLEAN COLLINS, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR.,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Whereas, it has been called to the attention of the Cook County Board of Com missioners that there is

legislation pending before the Illinois General Assembly, designed to provide greater protection of the
Miranda Rights of juvenile detainees, and
Whereas, the legislation further requires that interrogations be included in the video taping process in the

presence of legal counsel for the detainee, and
Whereas, the Cook County Board of Comm issioners is committed to protecting the rights of al l j uvenile
detainees and is currently considering ways within the scope of the Board's jurisdiction to insure greater
protection , and
Whereas, during the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Committee's deliberations on a similar

proposed County Ordinance the general consensus was the issue could be resolved at the State level, and
Whereas, some all eged juvenile confessions have been recanted due to practices employed in obtaining

the confession; subsequently, the Board was held liable for damages and monetary awards causing
unnecessary expenditure of tax dollars, now
T herefore, Be It Resolved, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners do hereby call upon the

Governor and the State Legislature to enact laws providing for the protection of juvenile detainee's
Miranda Rights, the appointment of legal counsel prior to interrogation and confessions when a juvenile
is detained in connection to a crime that could be classified as a Class I or above felony if committed by
an adult, and
Be It Further Resolved , that the Governor and the State Legislature provide for financial assistance to
local units of government where there is a disproportionate number of juvenile crime and that a copy of
this Resolution be given to the Speaker of the House and Minority Leader, the President of the Senate and
Minority Spokesman.

1066

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MARCH 9, 2000
Approved and adopted this 9th day of March 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted, as amended. The motion carried unanimously.
